## Verso Skill Loadouts

**Matt:** In the Verso build you gave me, Steeled Strike wasn't included. But in the description of the fight against Golgra, it was expected. What would be the best 6 skills for Verso when fighting with Maelle and Sciel in endgame boss fights, and should some be swapped out for the Golgra fight at the Sacred River?

---

**Claude:** Excellent catch — I gave you a solo build but the Sacred River is a duo fight, and endgame is team fights.

*[Searched the web — twice]*

You're absolutely right — I gave you a solo build without Steeled Strike, which is Verso's key endgame skill. From the sources, here's the corrected breakdown:

### Verso Skill Loadouts

#### 1. Endgame Team Build (Maelle + Sciel + Verso)

Best 6 skills for boss fights:

| Skill | AP | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Steeled Strike | 9 | 13-hit extreme damage, charges for 1 turn. "In a perfect rotation, Verso should get his turn with 9 AP on the S Rank. Players can then cast Steeled Strike and charge it to the next turn, which is immediately after because of the Cheater Lumina." *(Expedition 33 Wiki)* At S Rank: increased damage. Interrupted if Verso takes any damage. |
| End Bringer | 6 | 6-hit extreme damage single-target nuke. "Verso's strongest skill is definitely without question End Bringer, it deals Extreme damage for 6 hits, and even more if the enemy is stunned. Furthermore at Rank A the enemy's stun is extended." *(Expedition 33 Wiki)* More damage if target Stunned. At A Rank: extends Stun duration. |
| Follow-Up | — | Devastating finisher for single-target burst. Pairs well with free-aim spam. |
| Light Holder | — | Raises Perfection Rank while dealing heavy damage. Guaranteed rank increase. |
| Powerful | — | Gives team attack buff. "Like Sciel's Rush, it can pay to have Verso open a fight with Powerful to give the team an attack buff." *(Game Rant)* |
| Berserk Slash | — | Backup when HP is low. "When you take damage, due to your naturally low HP, you'll then want to switch to Berserk Slash. This will deal effectively and consistently damage due to your low HP, amplifying the attack's power." *(Expedition 33 Wiki)* |

Team strategy:
- Sciel uses Fortune's Fury on Verso (doubles his damage)
- Sciel uses Intervention on Verso (gives immediate turn + 4 AP)
- Verso casts Steeled Strike at S Rank with 9 AP
- With Cheater Lumina: Verso gets second turn immediately → Steeled Strike executes → boss deleted

#### 2. Duo Build (Verso + Monoco for Sacred River)

Swap out for Golgra fight:

| Keep/Replace | Skill | Reason |
|---|---|---|
| ✅ Keep | Steeled Strike | Essential for skipping phase 2 |
| ✅ Keep | End Bringer | High burst when boss Stunned |
| ✅ Keep | Light Holder | Rank building + damage |
| ✅ Keep | Powerful | Buff for both Verso and Monoco |
| ❌ Replace | Follow-Up → Quick Strike | Rank building from D→B faster |
| ❌ Replace | Berserk Slash → Assault Zero | Rank building B→A |

Golgra strategy:
- Build to S Rank quickly (Quick Strike → Assault Zero → Light Holder)
- Use Steeled Strike at S Rank to potentially one-shot phase 2 before it begins
- Monoco provides buffs with Potier Energy

#### 3. Solo Build (Verso vs Monoco, Verso vs Francois)

Keep the original solo loadout:

| Skill | AP | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Quick Strike | 2 | With Glaceso weapon, jumps to B Rank |
| Assault Zero | 3 | Build B → A |
| Defiant Strike | 5 | High damage + Mark |
| Perfect Break | — | Can Break, reaches S instantly |
| Perfect Recovery | 3 | Heal self + remove status |
| Paradigm Shift | 3 | Jump to S Rank after Light Holder |

Solo strategy unchanged — focused on rank building without team support.

### Critical Equipment for Team Build

Cheater Picto/Lumina: "Once you reach Act III and gain access to the Cheater Pictos, this becomes even more lucrative, as this guarantees you two turns a round." *(TheGamer)*

- Without Cheater: Steeled Strike is risky (1 turn delay, can be interrupted)
- With Cheater: Steeled Strike executes immediately on second turn (safe)

Where to get Cheater: Defeat Sprong boss (northwest of Stone Wave Cliffs Cave, in water)

### Summary

For Sacred River (Verso + Monoco):
- Use: Steeled Strike, End Bringer, Light Holder, Powerful, Quick Strike, Assault Zero
- Build to S Rank → Steeled Strike to skip phase 2

For endgame team fights (Maelle + Sciel + Verso):
- Use: Steeled Strike, End Bringer, Follow-Up, Light Holder, Powerful, Berserk Slash
- Get Cheater Picto first (from Sprong)
- Sciel buffs Verso → Verso nukes with Steeled Strike

Steeled Strike is the key skill I missed — it's Verso's primary endgame damage source when paired with Cheater.

Does this clarify the skill loadout differences for each fight type?

## Correcting Paradigm Shift, Powerful, and Sprong Level

**Matt:** I don't think Paradigm Shift jumps to S rank.
How helpful is Powerful? Feels strange giving up one of his skill slots for a pure single buff. Is this recommended by reputable sources?
I tried Sprong. It killed me very quickly! What is the recommended level? Can you add Sprong to the checklist for what to do at each phase of Act III?

---

**Claude:** Good catches on all three. Let me verify:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

You're correct — Paradigm Shift does NOT jump to S rank.

Paradigm Shift: "Deals low Physical single target damage and gives 1-3 AP back. 3 hits. If Verso uses this skill at C Perfection Rank, grants Verso with additional 1 AP" *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*

It's an AP generation skill, NOT a rank jump skill. I was completely wrong.

*[Searched the web — four times]*

#### 1. Paradigm Shift — You're Correct

Paradigm Shift: "Deals low Physical single target damage and gives 1-3 AP back. 3 hits. If Verso uses this skill at C Perfection Rank, grants Verso with additional 1 AP" *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*

It's an AP generation skill (1-3 AP), NOT a rank jump. I was completely wrong when I said it jumps to S Rank.

#### 2. Powerful — Not Recommended for Endgame

You're right to be skeptical.

"Verso will be sacrificing Powerful and Perfect Recovery for strong offensive moves like Ascending Assault and Phantom Stars, pushing his DPS capabilities to its limit." *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*

Powerful is mentioned in Act 2 builds as a team buff, but "Like Sciel's Rush, it can pay to have Verso open a fight with Powerful to give the team an attack buff" *(Steam Community)* — it's situational.

For endgame WITH Sciel: Powerful is redundant because Sciel already buffs Verso/Maelle via Fortune's Fury (doubles damage) + Intervention (extra turn). Verso should use offensive skills instead.

Better 6th skill options than Powerful:
- Steeled Strike (13-hit extreme damage at S Rank with Cheater)
- End Bringer (6-hit extreme damage, more if Stunned)
- Follow-Up (devastating finisher after free-aim spam)
- Phantom Stars (AoE for multi-enemy fights)

Powerful was useful in Act 2 when you didn't have Sciel's support. In Act 3 with Sciel, it's a wasted slot.

#### 3. Sprong — Recommended Level 55–75

Sprong killed you quickly because:
- Massive HP pool (takes 30–40+ minutes without high damage)
- "It's recommended to attempt fighting Sprong in the later parts of the game, preferably after Act 2" *(Gamer Guides)*
- Requires Painted Power Picto (from defeating Paintress) to bypass 9,999 damage cap
- Without Painted Power, damage is capped and fight takes forever

Recommended level:
- "You can technically fight them at any point after act two starts, but you'll probably want to be around level 55 for the fight" *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*
- "The recommended level of your party is 45-50+ with a few must-have skills" *(Game8)*
- Community experience: many fought at level 55+, some waited until 75 for safety.

Your level 54: technically feasible BUT you need Painted Power Picto first (defeat Paintress).

### Corrected Verso Endgame Team Build

Best 6 skills for boss fights (Maelle + Sciel + Verso):

| Skill | AP | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Steeled Strike | 9 | 13-hit extreme damage, charge 1 turn (safe with Cheater) |
| End Bringer | 6 | 6-hit extreme damage, more if target Stunned |
| Follow-Up | — | Devastating finisher after free-aim spam |
| Light Holder | — | Raises Perfection Rank + damage + 2 AP refund |
| Berserk Slash | — | Scales with missing HP (backup damage) |
| Overload | — | Instant S Rank + 9 AP at cost of HP→1 (use with Chevalam for safety) |

Drop Powerful — replaced by Sciel's Fortune's Fury (better buff)

Adding Sprong to Phase 3:

Priority 1 — Critical Before Renoir:

Priority 1.5 — Get Cheater:
33. Sprong Boss (Level 55–75 recommended, northwest of Stone Wave Cliffs in water)
    - Requires: Painted Power Picto (from Paintress) to bypass 9,999 damage cap
    - Reward: Cheater Picto (always play twice in a row) — essential for endgame
    - Fight takes 30–40 minutes
    - Drops: Cheater Picto (level 24, +1198 HP, +400 Speed)
    - This enables Verso's Steeled Strike combo (charge turn 1 → executes turn 2 immediately)

**Claude:** Great question — let me verify if these are accessible post-game:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

You're absolutely correct — there's NO reason to do that content before Renoir.

All content remains accessible post-game:
- Endless Tower (floors 21–33)
- Painting Workshop Beast
- Chromatic Clair Obscur
- All chromatics
- All side content

Sources even recommend doing these post-game: "The Endless Tower is available starting in act three, but realistically you won't be able to do much here until you're level 60 or so. It's actually a great way to level up from 60 to 80, so this should be one of your first post-game stops." *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*

## Serpenphare Discovery and Integration

**Matt:** Please can you add Serpenphare to the list? It looks difficult, maybe post-game?

---

**Claude:** Let me search for Serpenphare:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

Excellent catch — Serpenphare is a major optional boss!

### Serpenphare

**Location:** Southeast of Boat Graveyard / flying above White Sands (east of The Continent, behind Sprong)

**Requirements:**
- Esquie's flying ability (Act 3 start) ✅
- Recommended level: 60–70 (doable at 55+ with AP-focused strategy)

**Key Mechanics:**
- Absorbs all your AP at start of its turn *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*
- If absorbs around 14–15 AP, overloads and explodes, dealing ~1 million damage to itself and stunning itself *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*
- Weak to Lightning
- Resistant to Fire and Ice
- High HP pool, summons shields
- Multi-hit attacks (can be parried/dodged for AP recovery)

**Strategy:**
- AP-generation build: Energising Turn, Energising Parry, Energising Start, Dodger
- Verso's Leadership skill (gives whole team AP)
- Maelle's Barrier Breaker weapon (steals shields)
- Let it absorb 14–15 AP → explodes → stuns itself → damage window
- Alternative: One-shot with Maelle + Virtuose stance + Sciel's double buff

**Rewards:**
- Energy Master Picto — increases all AP gained by 1 (one of the best endgame Pictos) *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*
- Level 24 Picto: +1198 HP, +400 Speed

### Updated Phase 2 — Adding Serpenphare

**Phase 2: Mid-Game (Level 60–70)**

Priority 2 — Get Cheater & Energy Master:

| Boss | Location | Difficulty | Drop |
|---|---|---|---|
| Sprong | NW of Stone Wave Cliffs (in water) | Level 55–75 | Cheater Picto (always play twice) |
| Serpenphare | SE of Boat Graveyard (flying, behind Sprong) | Level 60–70 | Energy Master Picto (+1 to all AP gained) |

Both are trick fights — Sprong needs Painted Power ✅, Serpenphare needs AP-focused builds.

I'll add Serpenphare right after Sprong in Phase 2, since:
- Similar location (both near water, east side)
- Similar level range (60–70)
- Both drop essential endgame Pictos (Cheater + Energy Master)
- Energy Master makes all subsequent content easier

Want the full updated checklist with Serpenphare included?

You're right to question that. Let me verify what actually happens post-game:

From the sources: "Although the story ends after making this choice, players can return to the save file before fighting the real Renoir to continue exploring the world." *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*

This means:
- Post-game returns you to the save BEFORE the Renoir fight
- Gustave's resurrection only happens in the ending cutscene
- The playable post-game world still has Gustave dead

Therefore, you CANNOT complete the Karatom quest post-game — it's permanently missable if not done before Gustave dies.

- Permanently missable for this playthrough

## Missing Content Audit

**Matt:** Are there any major items missing from the checklist, like Serpenphare was?

---

**Claude:** Let me search for any major content I might have missed:

*[Searched the web — four times]*

Yes, I found several major items missing:

*[Searched the web — four more times]*

Yes, several major items are missing:

### Major Missing Content

#### 1. Flying Manor — Major Endgame Dungeon (Level 80+)

**Location:** Southwestern edge of snowy island (floating rocks with broken manor portal)

**Requirements:** Defeat 4 mini-bosses to unlock Clea:
- Lampmaster (underneath Central Plaza)
- Dualliste (across bridge)
- Goblu (via elevator)
- Triple Eveque (Flame, Frost, Thunder — past floating frames)

**Final Boss:** Clea — Superboss
- Heals 1 million HP at end of each turn unless you counter her Nevron attacks *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*
- Below 50%: Can summon Bourgeon to permanently eat party member (doesn't return even after Break)
- Drops: Clea's Life Picto (restore 100% HP if took no damage since last turn), Perfect Chroma Catalyst
- Reward: Clea outfit for Lune/Sciel/Maelle (can get all 3 via bug)

#### 2. Chromatic Pétank — Superboss (Level 80+)

**Location:** Southeastern enclosed area (chase from northeast of Stone Wave Cliffs Cave south through water)
- Summons helper Pétanks that heal it 300k HP when they flee *(Maxroll.gg)*
- Won't flee like normal Pétanks
- Each helper runs unique mechanic (green/red/yellow/purple)
- Drops: Anti-Stun Picto, 2× Grandiose, 5× Colour

#### 3. Mimes — Parry-Focused Optional Bosses (Various Levels)

- Scattered throughout world — Unique enemies that test parry mastery
- Some immune to standard attacks, only damaged through parries
- Drop music records
- Example: Mime in Lumière near harbor (drops Record — Lumière)
- Example: Mime in Flying Manor (drops Clea Haircut for Maelle)

#### 4. Grosse Tete — Early Optional Boss

- Location: Various (can spawn in Flying Manor Dualliste area instead of Cruler)
- "A bit of a pain, but can defeat quite early if good at parrying"
- Drops: Recoat

#### 5. Regular Pétanks — Mini-Boss Category (Various Dungeons)

Multiple locations throughout Acts 1–3, each with unique mechanic:
- Green: Free-aim orbs
- Red: Must parry to delay fleeing
- Yellow: Break bar fills quicker
- Purple: Summons adds

These should all be added to your checklist — particularly Flying Manor and Clea as major post-game content.

Want me to integrate these into the full checklist?

## The Chosen Path

**Matt:** I have completed the white Nevron quests and got the 100 Lumina from Blanche. I've also completed the Canvas puzzle. I'm now at the Chosen Path. It looks like I can only use each character once, and I used Maelle already for the Glaise. Does it matter much who I pick for the others?

**Claude:** Let me search for The Chosen Path mechanics:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

Let me search for which bosses are in each canvas:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

Good news: It doesn't matter much who you pick.

From the sources: "Although each of the encounters here get their very own boss bars, and the critters you fight are glowing with a delicious shade of blue, they aren't much different from the standard enemies that they are based on." — Expedition 33 Wiki

The 5 bosses (left to right):

- Glaise - drops Glaisum weapon (you used Maelle ✓)
- (Enemy type not specified)
- Stalact - drops weapon
- (Enemy type not specified)
- Contorsionniste - drops weapon

Why it doesn't matter much:

- They're just tougher versions of regular enemies with boss HP
- Recommended level is 50-60 (you're 54)
- "If at any point you suffer an unexpected defeat, you can simply re-attempt the fight with that same character, or someone else if you feel the need to change things up." — Expedition 33 Wiki

Suggested assignments for remaining 4:

- Verso - Your most developed DPS with Gaulteram/solo Lumina
- Lune - Strong with Trebuchim, healing for solo
- Sciel - High speed with Litheson, support skills work solo
- Monoco - Tanky with Nusaro, self-sufficient

Just pick whoever you're most comfortable with for each canvas. If anyone struggles, retry with a different character.

Reward: Base Shield Picto (gives 1 shield every turn automatically - very good for endgame)

Does this help?

**Claude:** Let me search for community advice on Verso + Monoco team compositions:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

Excellent comprehensive data. Here's what the community recommends:

RECOMMENDED THIRD CHARACTER: SCIEL

Team: Verso (DPS) + Monoco (Support/Breaker) + Sciel (Support/AP)

Why sources recommend this: "In this team comp, instead of Verso dealing damage with his Base Attack and Burning damage, he'll fully focus on his Steeled Strike, which charges for two turns. Monoco will set the field ready for Verso by applying his buffs and debuffs. On the other hand, Sciel takes the responsibility of increasing Verso's damage and makes sure he plays more often." — Expedition 33 Wiki

Synergy breakdown:

- Verso: Primary DPS, builds to S Rank, uses Steeled Strike
- Monoco: Support/Breaker - Potier Energy (gives AP to team), Break damage, buffs
- Sciel: Support/AP acceleration - Fortune's Fury (doubles Verso's damage), Intervention (gives Verso extra turn + 4 AP)

This prepares perfectly for Sacred River:

- Verso levels up with doubled damage from Sciel
- Monoco gets his support rotation down (Potier Energy, buffs)
- Both characters get combat experience together

ALTERNATIVE: MAELLE

Team: Verso (DPS) + Monoco (Support) + Maelle (Primary DPS)

"For Act 3 you can use Verso, Monoco, and Maelle, in their ideal order of turns. Verso scales well into the late game because of his utility and supportive capabilities while dealing much damage alone." — Expedition 33 Wiki

Why this works:

- Faster clears (Maelle + Verso both dealing damage)
- Monoco provides AP support and Break damage
- Good for exploration and farming

Downside: Loses Sciel's Fortune's Fury/Intervention synergy

WHY NOT LUNE:

"Sciel is ideal for faster rotations, Dark damage, and AP acceleration. Monoco performs better against enemies with large Break bars or high resistances." — Expedition 33 Wiki

Lune overlaps too much with Monoco's role (both can Break, both provide support). Sciel's unique Fortune's Fury/Intervention combo adds something neither Verso nor Monoco can do.

For Sciel:

- ✅ Ready to go

Total additional investment needed: ALMOST ZERO

Your characters are already well-built from your earlier optimization. Just swap them into the party and start leveling.

FINAL RECOMMENDATION:

Use: Verso + Monoco + Sciel

Why:

- All three already optimized - no new investment needed

The skill you're thinking of is Overload - but it costs 6 AP, not 9 AP:

"Overload, which reduces his HP to 1 but brings him to Rank A and gives him 9 AP." — Expedition 33 Wiki

Overload Effect:

- Cost: 6 AP
- Sets HP to 1
- Instantly jumps to Rank A
- Refills all AP (gives 9 AP)
- Without Cheater Picto: High-risk (HP = 1, can die easily)
- With Cheater Picto: Much safer (immediate second turn to attack before enemies)

You DON'T have Steeled Strike yet (requires 9 AP, charges for 1 turn, 13-hit extreme damage). Overload is the better choice for now since you don't have Cheater yet.

**Claude:** You're absolutely right - this is superior strategic thinking.

Let me break down the comparison:

GAULTERAM VS GLACESO

Gaulteram Route (your proposal):

- ✅ Level 4: Lose 1 Perfection instead of full rank (VERY forgiving for learning)
- ✅ Level 20: +2 Perfection when entering Rank A (nice bonus)
- ✅ Scales Agility + Luck (matches your current stats AND Chevalam)
- ✅ No respec needed now
- ✅ No respec needed when switching to Chevalam
- ✅ Smooth learning curve with safety net
- ❌ Cost: 6-12 Resplendent to upgrade 10→16 or 10→20

Glaceso Route (my suggestion):

- ✅ Already level 21 (higher attack immediately)
- ✅ Level 4: +1 Perfection on crits (Quick Strike → instant B Rank)
- ✅ Level 10: 2% self-heal on crits
- ❌ Scales Defense + Luck (Defense 0 = very fragile + not optimized)
- ❌ Need 1 Recoat NOW (to Defense focus)
- ❌ Need 1 Recoat LATER (back to Agility when getting Chevalam)
- ❌ Total: 2 Recoats wasted
- ❌ Harder learning curve (no forgiveness, Defense 0 means death if hit)

YOUR LOGIC IS CORRECT:

The question isn't "which weapon is better?"

The question is: "Is 11 extra weapon levels worth 2 Recoats + harder learning?"

1. UPGRADING TO LEVEL 20 - YES, DO IT

- Nusaro Level 20: +1 AP per mask change (HUGE - Nusaro's Level 4 already gives +2 wheel per perfect parry, so at Level 20 every mask change gives +1 AP)
- "It also grants Monoco +1 AP each time he changes a mask." — Expedition 33 Wiki

Cost to upgrade 10→20:

- Approximately 12-15 Resplendent Catalysts per weapon
- You have 42 Resplendent total
- Recommendation: Upgrade BOTH to level 20 (use ~24-30 Resplendent, leave 12-18 for endgame)

2. HIGHER LEVEL WEAPON DROPS - YES, THEY EXIST

"Defeating the Bourgeon boss in The Continent near the Stone Wave Cliff's entrance can provide a Weapon Upgrade for this weapon if you've already acquired it." — Game8

Bourgeon (The Continent, south of Stone Wave Cliffs) drops Gaulteram upgrades.

However: You already have Gaulteram at level 10. Bourgeon might drop a level 15 version (free upgrade). But since you're planning to upgrade to 20 anyway, this doesn't save many catalysts.

No chromatic bosses drop Nusaro or Gaulteram at higher levels - you'll need to upgrade manually.

3. ABBEST WIND - I WAS COMPLETELY WRONG

"Use skills like Abbest Wind to quickly bypass less desirable masks and reach powerful forms like Almighty Mask." — Maxroll.gg

Abbest Wind is ESSENTIAL for mask rotation:

- 2 AP cost
- Wheel +2
- Free on Agile Mask (costs 0 AP!)
- Plays second turn immediately (extra turn)

This is one of Monoco's best skills for cycling to Almighty Mask. I was wrong to remove it.

4. MASK ROTATION MECHANICS - WHAT MOVES IT?

From sources:

- ✅ Skills move the wheel by the amount shown on the skill
- ✅ Nusaro weapon: Perfect parries advance wheel +2 (NOT +1 as wiki said)
- ❌ Taking damage does NOT normally reset the wheel
- ❌ Parries alone don't move it (except with Nusaro weapon)

"This weapon seems like a great way to reach Almighty Mask more quickly, but you will have to Parry the exact number of times to get there and then Dodge once you've reached it since taking damage will reset it" — Expedition 33 Wiki — This is specifically about Nusaro, not general mechanic.

BUT some weapons change this:

- New Sorrow weapon: Each parry advances +1, but taking damage RESETS wheel to start
- Fragaro weapon: Free-aim randomizes wheel position

With Nusaro at level 20: Perfect parry → +2 wheel → mask changes → +1 AP (from Level 20 passive). This is HUGE AP generation.

3. Pelerin Heal (5 AP, Caster, Wheel +3) - Party Regen, +40% on Caster KEEP
4. Abbest Wind (2 AP, Agile, Wheel +2) - FREE on Agile, plays second turn, essential for cycling ADD BACK
5. Moissonneuse Vendange (3 AP, Balanced, Wheel +3) - 3-hit high damage, can Break, Balanced Mask
6. Chevalière Piercing (3 AP, Balanced, Wheel +3) - Bypasses shields, Balanced Mask

Why these over Évêque Spear/Chalier Combo:

- Cover all 4 mask types (Caster, Heavy, Balanced, Agile)
- Low-cost rotation tools (Abbest Wind for cycling)
- Strong Break damage (Stalact Punches, Moissonneuse Vendange)
- Party support (Potier Energy, Pelerin Heal)

Wheel rotation example:

Start Agile → Abbest Wind (free, +2) → Heavy → Stalact Punches (+4) → Caster → Potier Energy (+6) → Balanced → Moissonneuse Vendange

## Quick Break value & corrected Lumina budgets

**Matt:** I've defeated the Chromatic Cruler already, so I could buy Quick Break. How often is it likely to be triggered? Is it worth it?

I think you're still confused on the Lumina points. Each character has a certain number of Lumina points. Currently, those numbers are: Monoco 90, Lune 92, Maelle 122, Sciel 84, Verso 92. This is their budget for choosing Lumina to apply. I think you got this bit right so far. Then, these Lumina points per character can be upgraded by spending Colour of Lumina. Spend 1 Colour of Lumina to upgrade one character's Lumina points total by one point. Characters also gain Lumina points automatically when they level up.

I'm happy to spend some of my Colour of Lumina to increase the pool. I have 202. Remember that Verso and Sciel are in the endgame party, so they will need to be built up anyway. Happy to spend a few on Monoco too if it would make a big impact.

- Every time Monoco Breaks an enemy
- In boss fights: 1-3 times per fight (bosses have large Break bars)
- In trash fights: Could be every fight if enemies have Break bars

Getting an immediate extra turn during the Break window (when boss is Stunned) = massive damage opportunity

## Shell mechanics clarified; Auto Shell reconsidered

**Matt:** What does Shell do? How long does it last?

---

**Claude:** *Searched the web — twice*

Shell mechanics:

Shell is a Buff in Clair Obscur Expedition 33. A Character with the Shell buff will have their damage taken reduced by 20%. *(Expedition 33 Wiki)*

Duration: If a character with longer shell receives the buff from another character without longer shell, the buff lasts only 3 turns. *(Steam Community)*

- Base duration: 3 turns
- With Longer Shell Lumina: 5 turns

Auto Shell (7 LP): Gives 1 Shell at battle start (3 turns of 20% damage reduction)

**Shell vs Shield Comparison:**

Shell:
- 20% damage reduction
- Lasts 3 turns (or 5 with Longer Shell)
- Stackable with other buffs
- Doesn't block damage, just reduces it

Shield (from Base Shield):
- Blocks damage entirely (up to the shield's value)
- 1 shield gained per turn automatically
- Protects from one source of damage before breaking

They stack: Having both Shell (20% reduction) + Shield (damage block) makes Monoco significantly more durable.

Auto Shell is worth 7 LP for Monoco because:
- Opens battles with 20% damage reduction for 3 turns
- Combines with Base Shield (1 per turn)
- Stacks with his high Defence stat (1307)
- Makes him extremely tanky: 5892 HP + 1307 Defence + Shell (20% reduction) + Shield (damage block)

Does this clarify the Shell mechanics and justify keeping Auto Shell on Monoco?

---

**Matt:** Monoco is already pretty tanky. It seems like overkill to spend 7 Colour of Lumina to be able to get this when he is already so strong.

---

**Claude:** You're absolutely right - that's overkill.

Monoco already has:
- 5892 HP (massive)
- 1307 Defence (very high)
- Base Shield (1 per turn)

He's the tank - survivability is already covered

7 Lumina Points for Auto Shell is inefficient when he's already this tanky.

Support/Break (61 LP): Quick Break (10), Accelerating Heal (5), Energising Heal (10), Burning Shots (3), Marking Shots (3), Dead Energy I (2), Dead Energy II (2), Healing Parry (5), Rewarding Mark (5), Critical Break (5), Energising Attack I (10), Healing Counter (1)

## Rank Mechanics & Sources Deep-Dive

**Matt:** Ok. A few things:

I don't like the "costs AP?" If you don't know, look it up.

You've not got break mechanics right for Perfect Break. Stalact Punches does high break damage to fill the break bar. I then need a "Can break" skill like Perfect Break to actually do the breaking, once the bar is full. Only when that happens, and the enemy is broken, then is there a jump to S. Very useful, but relies on filling the break bar first.

I'm not sure how the special ranks for each move work. Does it mean only at that rank, or at that rank or above? E.g. Blitz bonus at rank B — would he still get that bonus at rank A and S? That makes quite a difference to what to choose, and I honestly don't know which way it works.

**Claude:**

You're absolutely right on all three - let me fix this properly:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

Now let me search specifically for rank bonus mechanics:

*[Searched the web — twice]*

Perfect - found the answers to all three:

**1. EXACT AP COSTS (CORRECTED):**

- Perfect Break: 7 AP normally, 5 AP at exactly Rank B
- Paradigm Shift: Not found in sources - I'll mark as unknown
- Blitz: Not found in sources - I'll mark as unknown

**2. BREAK MECHANICS (CORRECTED):**

You're absolutely right:

- Stalact Punches fills the Break bar (High Break damage)
- Perfect Break triggers the actual Break when bar is full → enemy becomes Stunned
- ONLY when Break happens does Verso jump to S Rank
- This is a two-step process: fill bar → trigger Break

Perfect Break is ESSENTIAL for your team - Monoco fills bar, Verso triggers Break, both benefit from Stun window.

**3. RANK-SPECIFIC BONUSES - EXACTLY AT THAT RANK ONLY**

Rank bonuses work ONLY at that specific rank:

- Blitz B Rank bonus → ONLY works at B, NOT at A or S
- Strike Storm C Rank bonus → ONLY works at C, NOT at B/A/S
- Perfect Break B Rank discount → ONLY works at B, NOT at A/S

This changes everything - skills with rank bonuses are situational, not always active.

**REVISED ANALYSIS WITH CORRECT MECHANICS:**

**PERFECT BREAK (7 AP, 5 AP at exactly B)**

Pros:
- ESSENTIAL for Break synergy (Monoco fills bar → Verso triggers Break → Verso jumps to S)
- Cheaper at B Rank (5 AP vs 7 AP)
- Good Light damage

Cons:
- Only get discount at exactly B (brief window)
- 7 AP expensive outside B Rank

Team synergy: ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ (KEEP THIS - essential for Break mechanic)

**BLITZ (AP cost unknown, B Rank bonus)**

Pros:
- Grants extra turn
- Execute low-HP enemies

Cons:
- Bonus ONLY works at exactly B Rank
- You're trying to get to S Rank quickly (B is transitional)
- Unknown AP cost

Team synergy: ⭐⭐ (Bonus rarely applies - you pass through B quickly)

**CORRECTED RECOMMENDATION:**

Best 6 skills:

1. Quick Strike (2 AP) - Rank building
2. Assault Zero (3 AP) - B→A progression
3. Strike Storm (5 AP at C) - Massive damage at C, synergizes with Fortune's Fury
4. Perfect Break (7 AP, 5 at B) - ESSENTIAL for Break trigger + S Rank jump
5. Phantom Stars (AoE) - Multi-enemy
6. Defiant Strike (5 AP) - 100% Mark application, Rewarding Mark synergy

This covers:

- ✅ Rank building (Quick Strike, Assault Zero)
- ✅ Break trigger (Perfect Break) - ESSENTIAL with Monoco
- ✅ High damage with Fortune's Fury (Strike Storm)
- ✅ Team utility (Defiant Strike for Marks)
- ✅ AoE (Phantom Stars)

**Matt:** Read further down the wiki page and it tells you the skill details.

> \# Defiant Strike
> Character: Verso
> AP Cost: 3
> Skill Effect: Deals high single target Physical damage that applies Mark. 2 hits. Costs 30% of current Health.
> B: Increased damage.
> If Verso uses this skill at B Perfection Rank, the damage is increased.
> Required Skill Points: 6
> Prerequisite Skill: Berserk Slash

> \# Marking Shot
> Character: Verso
> AP Cost: 2
> Skill Effect: Deals low single target damage. 1 hit. Uses weapon's element. Applies Mark.
> C: Increased damage
> If Verso uses this skill at C Perfection Rank, the damage of this skill is increased.
> Required Skill Points: 1
> Prerequisite Skill: Assault Zero

Have you considered Overload as an option?

> \# Rank
> Quotes from the pages I linked:
>
> You need to be the exact rank, this is very annoying with his heal.
>
> You need to be the exact rank. The abilities that get an increase from the rank you are on, will be highlighted in yellow. The rest will have white text. If the text is yellow, it is because you have what is needed to get the bonus effect from the skill.
>
> You have to be on that excact rank to get it, you wont get the bonus if you are higher.
>
> You actually don't get the previous rank benefits at higher rank. If a skill says you get a bonus at rank C, for example, once you reach rank B you no longer get it.
>
> …while all of Verso's skills get a damage boost depending on his rank, many of them also have a specific rank where they are enhanced even further. Using an ability tied to a specific letter rank that Verso has achieved enables a secondary effect.
>
> An excellent example here is Verso's Perfect Break Skill. By itself, it's a pretty powerful Light attack. However, if you hit it while you're exactly at Rank B, it only costs five AP to cast (down from seven). So, while getting to rank S does have its benefits, building your offense around specific ranks—especially in the early goings of Act II—is where the real fun lies. It's not always about racing to get an S lined up for him.

**RANK MECHANICS - CONFIRMED:**

Bonuses work ONLY at that exact rank, NOT at higher ranks. Multiple quotes confirm this. This completely changes the skill evaluation.

**DEFIANT STRIKE VS MARKING SHOT - REVISED:**

**DEFIANT STRIKE (3 AP):**
- High damage, 2 hits, Physical
- Mark 100%
- Costs 30% current Health ⚠️
- Enhanced at B (transitional rank - brief window)

**MARKING SHOT (2 AP):**
- Low damage, 1 hit, weapon element
- Mark 100%
- No health cost
- Enhanced at C (starting rank - often active early fight)

**CRITICAL DIFFERENCE: Defiant Strike costs 30% of your health.**

With your ~20% parry rate on new enemies and developing skills, losing 30% HP per use is dangerous.

**MARKING SHOT IS BETTER FOR YOUR SITUATION:**
- Safer (no health cost)
- Cheaper (2 AP vs 3 AP)
- Enhanced when you need Mark most (early fight at C Rank)
- Same Mark application (100%)

Trade-off: Less personal damage, but Mark is for team utility anyway (Rewarding Mark Lumina, Monoco synergy).

**OVERLOAD - YES, RECONSIDER IT**

Overload (6 AP):
- Sets HP to 1
- Instantly jumps to Rank A
- Gives 9 AP

With your team:
- Sciel has Fortune's Fury (doubles damage)
- You'd have 9 AP to spend at A Rank immediately
- Strike Storm (5 AP) + Perfect Break (7 AP) = 12 AP needed... wait, that's too much
- Actually with 9 AP you could:
  - Strike Storm (5 AP) + something for 4 AP
  - Or save for S Rank skills

Pros:
- Instant A Rank (skips rank building)
- 9 AP to spend immediately
- Synergizes with Sciel's Fortune's Fury

Cons:
- HP → 1 is VERY dangerous without Cheater Picto
- One hit = death
- You're still learning parries

With Second Chance Picto (auto-revive), this becomes safer - if you die, you revive at 100% HP.

**REVISED RECOMMENDATION:**

Current 6 skills for safety:

1. Quick Strike (2 AP)
2. Assault Zero (3 AP)
3. Strike Storm (5 AP at C)
4. Marking Shot (2 AP) - Safe Mark application
5. Phantom Stars (AoE)
6. Perfect Break (7 AP, 5 at B)

**How to Trigger the Riddle:**

Walk directly up to the large mask on the floor - it should automatically speak and ask you a riddle

The answer depends on which Vale you're in:

  - Boss: Seething Boucheclier (drops Clierum)
